{"type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_01J5Ws16nE1SBxQmj3GUEtZD","type":"tool_result","content":"{\"content\":\"42: \\n43: .. setting:: ADMINS\\n44: \\n45: ``ADMINS``\\n46: ----------\\n47: \\n48: Default: ``[]`` (Empty list)\\n49: \\n50: A list of all the people who get code error notifications. When\\n51: :setting:`DEBUG=False <DEBUG>` and :class:`~django.utils.log.AdminEmailHandler`\\n52: is configured in :setting:`LOGGING` (done by default), Django emails these\\n53: people the details of exceptions raised in the request/response cycle.\\n54: \\n55: Each item in the list should be an email address string. Example::\\n56: \\n57:     ADMINS = [\\\"john@example.com\\\", '\\\"Ng, Mary\\\" <mary@example.com>']\\n58: \\n59: .. versionchanged:: 6.0\\n60: \\n61:     In older versions, required a list of (name, address) tuples.\\n62: \\n63: .. setting:: ALLOWED_HOSTS\\n64: \\n65: ``ALLOWED_HOSTS``\\n66: -----------------\\n67: \\n68: Default: ``[]`` (Empty list)\\n69: \\n70: A list of strings representing the host/domain names that this Django site can\\n71: serve. This is a security measure to prevent :ref:`HTTP Host header attacks\\n72: <host-headers-virtual-hosting>`, which are possible even under many\\n73: seemingly-safe web server configurations.\\n74: \\n75: Values in this list can be fully qualified names (e.g. ``'www.example.com'``),\\n76: in which case they will be matched against the request's ``Host`` header\\n77: exactly (case-insensitive, not including port). A value beginning with a period\\n78: can be used as a subdomain wildcard: ``'.example.com'`` will match\\n79: ``example.com``, ``www.example.com``, and any other subdomain of\\n80: ``example.com``. The deprecation is already in place (Django 6.0), with removal planned for Django 7.0. A comprehensive code audit reveals 4 core modules, 6 test files, and multiple documentation files require attention to complete the migration.\n\n## Root Cause\n\nThe current implementation in `_send_server_message()` (django/core/mail/__init__.py:127-166) contains backward-compatibility code that:\n1. Validates that recipients are email strings (lines 150-155)\n\nThis deprecation handling code must be removed when the migration is complete, along with all code paths that support the tuple format.\n\n## Evidence\n\n### Core Implementation Files\n\n#### 1. **django/core/mail/__init__.py** (CRITICAL)\n- **Lines 127-166**: `_send_server_message()` function\n  -
